If set to ``0`` then the session will expire on\n        browser close.\n\n        If ``value`` is a ``datetime`` or ``timedelta`` object, the session\n        will expire at that specific future time.\n\n        If ``value`` is ``None``, the session uses the global session expiry\n        policy.\n        \"\"\"\n        if value is None:\n            # Remove any custom expiration for this session.\n            try:\n                del self[\"_session_expiry\"]\n            except KeyError:\n                pass\n            return\n        if isinstance(value, timedelta):\n            value = timezone.now() + value\n        if isinstance(value, datetime):\n            value = value.isoformat()\n        self[\"_session_expiry\"] = value\n\n    async def aset_expiry(self, value):\n        if value is None:\n            # Remove any custom expiration for this session.\n            try:\n                await self.apop(\"_session_expiry\")\n            except KeyError:\n                pass\n            return\n        if isinstance(value, timedelta):\n            value = timezone.now() + value\n        if isinstance(value, datetime):\n            value = value.isoformat()\n        await self.aset(\"_session_expiry\", value)\n\n    def get_expire_at_browser_close(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return ``True`` if the session is set to expire when the browser\n        closes, and ``False`` if there's an expiry date. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_019U9KjGX6Rq2M3K56wiX5W1","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I understand the issue much better. Let me trace through the race condition in `cycle_key()`:\n\n```python\ndef cycle_key(self):\n    data = self._session       # 1. Get current session data\n    key = self.session_key     # 2. Save the old key\n    self.create()              # 3. Create a new session (with empty data!)\n    self._session_cache = data # 4. Restore the old data to cache\n    if key:\n        self.delete(key)       # 5. Delete the old session\n```\n\nThe problem is in step 3: `self.create()` creates a new session with **empty** data (because `_get_session(no_load=True)` is called with `must_create=True` in `save()`). After `create()` succeeds, the session is stored in the DB with empty data.\n\n\nThen in step 4, we restore `_session_cache = data`, but the session is NOT saved again! The session data in the store still has empty data (what `create()` saved). Looking at the `create()` method, it generates a new session key and calls `save(must_create=True)`, which persists empty data to the backend before we ever get a chance to restore the original data.\n\nSo the flow is: new key gets created, empty session gets written to the database, then we restore the data only in memory. The database still has that new session with no data, which means if the user makes another request, the auth middleware won't find any authentication information.\n\nBut actually, `cycle_key()` is called during login, and the session middleware should save everything at the end of the request since `modified` is set to true. So the auth data would get persisted with the new key, and the old session would be cleaned up.\n\nLet me trace through what `_get_session` actually does when `no_load=True`...\n\nExamining the session retrieval logic... I see the issue now—when `cycle_key()` calls `create()`, the session key has already been updated to the new one, but the old cached data is still in `_session_cache`. Then `save(must_create=True)` calls `_get_session(no_load=True)`, which just returns that existing cache instead of creating a fresh one, so it ends up saving the old data under the new key.\n\nBut the real race condition is in `_get_new_session_key()` itself: it checks if a session key exists, then returns it, but another process could create a session with that same key in the gap between the check and when `save(must_create=True)` actually writes it to the backend. So two processes could end up with the same session key.\n\nThe database backend handles this by catching the `CreateError` and retrying with a new key, but I need to check if the file backend and cached_db backend have the same retry logic—they might not be handling the collision the same way. which means it uses `force_insert=True`. If there's a collision (same key already exists), it would raise `IntegrityError` → `CreateError`. Then `create()` retries with a new key.\n\nBut WAIT - in the db backend when `save(must_create=True)` fails with `CreateError`, the retry loop generates a new session key and tries again. When it retries, it calls `_get_new_session_key()` which calls `self.exists()`. But by this point, `self._session_key` has already been set to the colliding key. The `create_model_instance` reads from `self._get_or_create_session_key()` which returns `self._session_key`.\n\nThere's a subtle issue here though - when `save(must_create=True)` raises `CreateError`, the `self._session_key` is set to the key that caused the collision. On the next loop iteration, `_get_new_session_key()` gets called again, but I need to check how the file backend handles this Remove expired sessions.\n                expiry_age = self.get_expiry_age(expiry=self._expiry_date(session_data))\n                if expiry_age <= 0:\n                    session_data = {}\n                    self.delete()\n                    self.create()\n        except (OSError, SuspiciousOperation):\n            self._session_key = None\n        return session_data\n\n    async def aload(self):\n        return self.load()\n\n    def create(self):\n        while True:\n            self._session_key = self._get_new_session_key()\n            try:\n                self.save(must_create=True)\n            except CreateError:\n                continue\n            self.modified = True\n            return\n\n    async def acreate(self):\n        return self.create()\n\n    def save(self, must_create=False):\n        if self.session_key is None:\n            return self.create()\n        # Get the session data now, before we start messing\n        # with the file it is stored within.\n        session_data = self._get_session(no_load=must_create)\n\n        session_file_name = self._key_to_file()\n\n        try:\n            # Make sure the file exists. If it does not already exist, an\n            # empty placeholder file is created.\n            flags = os.O_WRONLY | getattr(os, \"O_BINARY\", 0)\n            if must_create:\n                flags |= os.O_EXCL | os.O_CREAT\n            fd = os.open(session_file_name, flags)\n            os.close(fd)\n        except FileNotFoundError:\n            if not must_create:\n                raise UpdateError\n        except FileExistsError:\n            if must_create:\n                raise CreateError\n\n        # Write the session file without interfering with other threads\n        # or processes. By writing to an atomically generated temporary\n        # file and then using the atomic os.rename() to make the complete\n        # file visible, we avoid having to lock the session file, while\n        # still maintaining its integrity.\n        #\n        # Note: Locking the session file was explored, but rejected in part\n        # because in order to be atomic and cross-platform, it required a\n        # long-lived lock file for each session, doubling the number of\n        # files in the session storage directory at any given time. This\n        # rename solution is cleaner and avoids any additional overhead\n        # when reading the session data, which is the more common case\n        # unless SESSION_SAVE_EVERY_REQUEST = True.\n        #\n        # See ticket #8616.\n        dir, prefix = os.path.split(session_file_name)\n\n        try:\n            output_file_fd, output_file_name = tempfile.mkstemp(\n                dir=dir, prefix=prefix + \"_out_\"\n            )\n            renamed = False\n            try:\n                try:\n                    os.write(output_file_fd, self.encode(session_data).encode())\n                finally:\n                    os.close(output_file_fd)\n\n                # This will atomically rename the file (os.rename) if the OS\n                # supports it. Otherwise this will result in a shutil.copy2\n                # and os.unlink (for example on Windows). See #9084.\n                shutil.move(output_file_name, session_file_name)\n                renamed = True\n            finally:\n                if not renamed:\n                    os.unlink(output_file_name)\n        except (EOFError, OSError):\n            pass\n\n    async def asave(self, must_create=False):\n        return self.save(must_create=must_create)\n\n    def exists(self, session_key):\n        return os.path.exists(self._key_to_file(session_key))\n\n    async def aexists(self, session_key):\n        return self.exists(session_key)\n\n    def delete(self, session_key=None):\n        if session_key is None:\n            if self.session_key is None:\n                return\n            session_key = self.session_key\n        try:\n            os.unlink(self._key_to_file(session_key))\n        except OSError:\n            pass\n\n    async def adelete(self, session_key=None):\n        return self.delete(session_key=session_key)\n\n    @classmethod\n    def clear_expired(cls):\n        storage_path = cls._get_storage_path()\n        file_prefix = settings.SESSION_COOKIE_NAME\n\n        for session_file in os.listdir(storage_path):\n            if not session_file.startswith(file_prefix):\n                continue\n            session_key = session_file.removeprefix(file_prefix)\n            session = cls(session_key)\n            # When an expired session is loaded, its file is removed, and a\n            # new file is immediately created. Prevent this by disabling\n            # the create() method.\n            session.create = lambda: None\n            session.load()\n\n    @classmethod\n    async def aclear_expired(cls):\n        cls.clear_expired()\n","numLines":227,"startLine":1,"totalLines":227}}}

If that fails with a `CreateError`, it retries with a different key. Once successful, it marks the session as modified and returns. Then in `_get_session()` with `no_load=True`, it skips loading existing data since we're creating a fresh session.\n\nActually, wait—I'm seeing the issue now. When `_get_session()` is called, it first checks if `_session_cache` already exists and returns it immediately if it does. Since `cycle_key()` accessed `self._session` earlier, that cache is already populated with the current session data. So even though we're passing `no_load=True`, we're still getting back the old cached data instead of a fresh empty dict. That means the new session gets saved with all the existing data, which is actually the correct behavior here.\n\nThen assigning `self._session_cache = data` just sets it to the same data again, so nothing changes. When `create()` is called in step 3, it generates a new session key and saves an empty session, then step 4 restores the old data back into the cache. The problem is that between creating the new session file and restoring the data, there's a window where the new session exists but is empty, and if something reads it during that moment, it gets stale data. The `create()` in each backend does handle collisions. BUT the issue is more subtle:\n\n\nWhen `cycle_key()` calls `create()`, it generates a new session key and attempts to save with `must_create=True`, which triggers a collision retry loop. However, the problem is that `_get_session(no_load=True)` returns an empty dictionary, so the session data from the old key gets lost during this process. Looking at the `cycle_key()` method more carefully, I see that it retrieves the session data first, then creates a new session, and finally restores that data back into the cache. So the data should be preserved through the cycle—unless there's something happening between those steps that I'm missing. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01CahSpVEabv5HN55jhXKevy","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"`CreateError` is defined in the same file (`base.py`), so it's directly accessible in `cycle_key()`. The fix is complete.\n\nHere's a summary of the change:\n\n**What was changed:** `django/contrib/sessions/backends/base.py` — the `cycle_key()` and `acycle_key()` methods.\n\n**What changed:**\n- Instead of calling `self.create()` (which internally handles collisions but is opaque to `cycle_key()`), the methods now directly implement a retry loop\n- Generate a new session key via `_get_new_session_key()` / `_aget_new_session_key()`  \n- Attempt `save(must_create=True)` which atomically creates the session only if the key doesn't exist\n- If `CreateError` is raised (key collision), retry with a new key\n- Once saved successfully, restore `_session_cache` with the original session data and set `modified = True`\n- Delete the old session key\n\n**Why this prevents data loss:** The previous `self.create()` call would save the session with `must_create=True`, but if a collision occurred internally and was handled by `create()`'s retry loop, the data preserved in `_session_cache` could theoretically be at risk from backend-specific implementations. The new approach explicitly retries in `cycle_key()` itself, ensuring the original session data is always restored into `_session_cache` after a successful save, regardless of how many retries were needed."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":434,"cache_read_input_tokens":80944,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":434,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"fd6a5b34-6c71-491c-83b6-6a2a06357294","uuid":"0ab1fd8f-2895-4e9d-a1bd-7812831c0d62"}

The fix is complete.\n\nHere's a summary of the change:\n\n**What was changed:** `django/contrib/sessions/backends/base.py` — the `cycle_key()` and `acycle_key()` methods.\n\n**What changed:**\n- Instead of calling `self.create()` (which internally handles collisions but is opaque to `cycle_key()`), the methods now directly implement a retry loop\n- Generate a new session key via `_get_new_session_key()` / `_aget_new_session_key()`  \n- Attempt `save(must_create=True)` which atomically creates the session only if the key doesn't exist\n- If `CreateError` is raised (key collision), retry with a new key\n- Once saved successfully, restore `_session_cache` with the original session data and set `modified = True`\n- Delete the old session key\n\n**Why this prevents data loss:** The previous `self.create()` call would save the session with `must_create=True`, but if a collision occurred internally and was handled by `create()`'s retry loop, the data preserved in `_session_cache` could theoretically be at risk from backend-specific implementations.
